The process of getting my daughter's senior portraits taken went from frustrating to infuriating.  First of all, they are drastically marking up the price for senior portraits.  The lowest package costs $120 and that only includes one 8x10, two 5x7s, and eight wallets.   Of course, there is also a sitting fee, which means with tax you are going to pay almost $200 for the lowest package, with no touch-ups or extras.  The most expensive package with the sitting fee with set you back over $400.  You would think for all that money you would get amazing service, but even when I made an appointment I had to wait 20 minutes just to check in with someone and then another 40 minutes in a really crowded room for her actual appointment.  The sitting itself, which included a $50 sitting fee, was less than thirty minutes.  It might not be so appalling if the studio was not serving children in public schools whose parents probably can't afford to spend hundreds of dollars on photographs.  I still haven't been able to bring myself to actually buy the photographs because the price hiking is so troubling I'm actually considering taking it up with the school district.</Text>

<Text>John Adams Academy is a fantastic school! The idea that a child can receive a high quality liberal arts classical education at a tuition free public charter is an educational game changer.

The school board is experienced, principled, and in touch with the day to day operations of the school. They, along with administration, are always seeking to improve the quality of education offered to the scholars.

Like any school, John Adams Academy has challenges unique to its location, demographics, institutional type, and educational philosophy. <gmapID>0x809b1ff000000001:0x5f97c0a2c46e6695<//gmapID><userid>102623135370408395060<//userid><Name>Christian M<//Name><response>{'time': 1591305089558, 'text': 'Christian, Thank you so much for all of your servant leadership! We hope you have a great summer!'}< /response><Rate>4</Rate>< Review>
Student since the first year here! I have attended the school since fourth grade. I am now a Senior. I can honestly say that I love this school. The teachers are amazing (with a few exceptions, as with any school). They are honestly great people and take the time to get to know you personally. They will stop and ask how you are doing in the halls, make sure you don't need help on homework, and genuinely want to learn from the scholars as well as teach. The staff is friendly and helpful, and most of the scholars are nice and studious (we don't have bullying problems or much swearing because the majority of scholars are religious [LDS and Catholic are the two big ones]) Sadly, the administration is not as good, having a tendency toward unpreparedness and inconsistency. This is probably not the school for you if you don't enjoy a rigorous education. There are often philosophical discussions, debates, and socratic discussions, even in classes such as math and science. We don't have a great sports program unfortunately. However,  we have great music and art program and plenty of things to do if you are interested in debate, philosophy and a classic education. I highly recommend checking out the library.</Review>

< userid>
117861608990729120839< /userid>
<Pictures>None</Pictures>< Review>
Nice park in residential community. You do not see it from the main street.  In fact there is no sign showing park from main street. The park is completely fenced.  We entered thru the small gate in front.  Several slopes for walking up and down.  Also picnic tables located in different places.  Sandy playground with 2 swings for older kids and 2 for younger kids. No slides but a climbing area with bars and rope.  Stairs to walk across from side to side of the covered structure.  Have monkey bars in large circle formation and a very small zip line.  The zip line has no way for the kids to enter onto it.  You have to hold them up to reach the bar every time they want to use it.  (Only negative about the equipment). Great place to walk around and saw couple of older residences walking their dogs.  The residents can enter thru 2 other entrances from their streets and there is a water fountain. Grounds were very well maintained. No covered picnic area and no baseball field or basketball court. Nice park for the residential area and my 7 yr old great niece did enjoy playing there for about 2.5 hrs.</Review>

<user_id>114461558056437807671< /user_id><user_name>Shanon Yu</user_name>< Date>
1409183711019<//Date>
< rating>
3< /rating>
< Text>
If you want to let out your inner child, there's no better way then visiting Sky Zone indoor trampoline park!

I've heard so much about Sky Zone from friends and was thrilled when I saw that a Sky Zone was opening a couple miles way. This past weekend a group of my friends decided to take advantage of the $20 Saturday night deal for unlimited access from 9pm-12am (socks included, they usually charge $2 during regular hours).

The line was incredibly long when we arrived and to save time I highly suggest filling out the waiver beforehand. We waited about 20 minutes before we were able to pay admission and get our socks. Since we came during their Saturday night special, the place was extremely crowded and there were a bunch of kids everywhere. I definitely think I would have had a better experience if I came during off hours and were surrounded by people my own age.

Apparently the Covina Sky Zone is also smaller than some of the other locations. They have a dodgeball court, basketball area, foam pit, a general jumping area, and another area they closed off for private parties. When it got crowded, there were lines for everything and it took away from precious jumping time. I heard from my friends that the Anaheim location has two dodgeball courts so it could accommodate more people.

Overall I had an awesome time with my friends. Everyone should try Sky Zone at least once.  I also never thought jumping on trampolines could be so tiring. I definitely ran out of breath a couple times and had to rest quite a bit.

Tip* Leave valuables in your car. Lockers are available for 50 cents and there's a shoe rack  for you to place your belongings.< /Text>
